## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables map directly to a constitutive law relating stress (sigma) to strain (epsilon) with temperature (T) dependence, typical of thermoelasticity and elastoplastic/viscoplastic material models where stiffness and strength soften with increasing T and stress hardens with increasing strain.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain, isothermal elastic response)
- Thermoelastic stress with thermal strain subtraction: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain after thermal expansion)
- Linear temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus varies approximately linearly with T over a limited range)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate nonlinearity in elastic/total response)
- Nonlinear elastic with T-coupled coefficients: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (temperature alters tangent stiffness)
- Hollomon (power-law) hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic strain hardening after yielding, log-log linear behavior)
- Ludwik-type hardening (offset + power): sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield/initial stress plus strain hardening)
- Voce hardening (saturating): sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (hardening that approaches a saturation stress)
- Hyperbolic-tangent smooth yielding: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) (smooth transition from linear to plateau-like response without explicit piecewise yield)
- Johnson–Cook-like (no strain-rate term) with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T)**c4 (strain hardening combined with multiplicative thermal softening over a bounded T range)
- Multiplicative separable thermo-hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) * exp(c3 * T) (T-dependent scaling of the whole stress–strain curve)
- Rational softening with T and saturating with epsilon: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon))) / (1 + c3 * T) (strain hardening saturation while strength decreases with temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain linear elasticity shows up as sigma proportional to epsilon; the proportionality (slope) is the effective modulus and may vary with T.
- Thermal expansion effects often appear as an “effective strain” shift epsilon - c * (T - c0), producing stress-free strain at elevated temperature.
- Thermal softening commonly enters multiplicatively (e.g., sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T)), indicating that temperature scales the entire stress–strain response rather than adding an offset.
- Strain hardening that is approximately straight on log(sigma)–log(epsilon) plots suggests power-law forms in epsilon (epsilon**c).
- Saturation of hardening at large epsilon is naturally captured by 1 - exp(-c * epsilon) terms (approach to an asymptote).
- Smooth yield/transition behavior without explicit piecewise definitions is often represented by tanh(c * epsilon) or similar smooth limiting functions.
- If increasing T reduces both yield level and hardening rate, use T-dependent coefficients on both constant and epsilon-dependent terms (e.g., (c0 + c1*T) + (c2 + c3*T)*epsilon**c4).
- If sigma decreases roughly hyperbolically with T over a narrow range, rational factors like 1 / (1 + c * T) are a compact softening structure.

\[
23.7883415559\,\epsilon\big(-0.05042014461\,(T-330.2004199)+1\big)\;+\;5.2295006259\,\epsilon^{0.9585455289}(T-330.2004199)
\]
Rewrite into a clear “basis”:
- First term expands to \(A\,\epsilon + B\,T\epsilon\) (because \(\epsilon[-k(T-T_0)+1]=\epsilon(1+kT_0)-kT\epsilon\)).
- Second term is \(D\,T\,\epsilon^{p} + E\,\epsilon^{p}\) with \(p=0.9585455289\), since \(\epsilon^p(T-T_0)=T\epsilon^p - T_0\epsilon^p\).

So GT is exactly a linear combination of **four independent monomials**:
\[
(\epsilon),\quad (T\epsilon),\quad (\epsilon^{p}),\quad (T\epsilon^{p})
\]
with \(p\neq 1,2,\dots\) and no other \(T\)-dependence (no \(T\) alone, no constants, no logs/exps, no \(1/T\), etc.).

Now check candidates: a candidate can match only if it can represent **exactly** those four monomials and nothing else (extra terms must be zeroed), and it must include a \(T\epsilon^{p}\) term (this is the hardest requirement).

### 40. Rational form with denominator \((c2\epsilon+c3)\)
All \(T\)-dependence is \(T\) times something divided by \((c2\epsilon+c3)\). To match GT (a polynomial-like sum of monomials), the denominator must be constant: set \(c2=0\). Then expression becomes
\[
T(\alpha \epsilon^{c1}+\beta \epsilon^{c5})+\gamma \epsilon^{c1}+\delta \epsilon^{c8}
\]
This *can* produce \(T\epsilon\) and \(T\epsilon^{p}\) by setting \(c1=1\) and \(c5=p\). But then the non-\(T\) terms are \(\gamma \epsilon^{1}\) and \(\delta \epsilon^{c8}\). We need \(\epsilon\) and \(\epsilon^{p}\) (no other power). So set \(c8=p\). Then we have exactly:
\[
T(A\epsilon + B\epsilon^{p}) + C\epsilon + D\epsilon^{p}
\]
which matches the GT basis perfectly. Coefficients can be chosen to equal the GT’s four coefficients (and \(c3\neq 0\) just scales them; choose \(c3=1\) w.l.o.g.). Therefore **candidate 40 can match GT**.

(Concrete parameter choices exist: \(c2=0\), \(c3=1\), \(c1=1\), \(c5=0.9585455289\), \(c8=0.9585455289\), and choose \(c0,c4,c6,c7\) to match the four GT coefficients.)

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare each candidate to it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT expression is:
```
c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) + epsilon**c4*c5*(T - c6)
```

With c2 = c6 = 330.2004199209183, let me expand this:

```
c0*epsilon*(-c1*T + c1*c2 + c3) + c5*epsilon**c4*(T - c6)
```

Let me define new constants:
- Term 1: `c0*(-c1)*T*epsilon + c0*(c1*c2 + c3)*epsilon`
- Term 2: `c5*T*epsilon**c4 - c5*c6*epsilon**c4`

So GT = `A*T*epsilon + B*epsilon + C*T*epsilon**c4 + D*epsilon**c4`

Where:
- A = c0*(-c1) = 23.788... * (-0.05042...) = -1.1994...
- B = c0*(c1*c2 + c3) = 23.788... * (0.05042*330.2 + 1) = 23.788*(16.645 + 1) = 23.788*17.645 ≈ 419.76
- C = c5 = 5.2295
- D = -c5*c6 = -5.2295*330.2 = -1726.8
- c4 = 0.9585...

So GT has the form:
**GT = A·T·ε + B·ε + C·T·ε^p + D·ε^p**

where p ≈ 0.9585.

The basis functions are: {T·ε, ε, T·ε^p, ε^p} with p as a free exponent.

Now let me check each candidate.

### Candidate 1: `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + c2*epsilon**2 + c3 + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon + c7*epsilon**c8`

Basis: {T·ε, T, ε², 1, ε^c5, ε, ε^c8}

GT needs T·ε^p term. This candidate has no T·ε^p term. The T dependence only appears as T·ε and T (constant in ε). GT requires T coupled with ε^p, which isn't available here. Setting c1=0 removes T, but then we lose the T·ε^p term entirely.

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]
